# Kafka Consumer Group Protocol State Machine

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the consumer group coordinator's state machine, including the Join, Sync, and Rebalance states and the transitions between them.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

1. Files defining state enums or state classes for consumer groups, particularly those with states related to "Join", "Sync", "Rebalance", "ASSIGNING", "RECONCILING", "EMPTY", "STABLE" or similar

- org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/consumer/
- org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/
- Files with "Group" or "State" or "Protocol" in their names

Return the file paths of all relevant Java source files that define or use the consumer group state machine.

   992→        assertValidTransition(groupState);
   993→        previousState = state;

   997→
   998→    /**
   999→     * Select a protocol that will be used for this group. Each member
  1000→     * will vote for a protocol and the one with the most votes will
  1001→     * be selected. Only a protocol that is supported by all members
  1002→     * can be selected.
  1003→     *
  1004→     * @return the name of the selected protocol.
  1005→     */
  1006→    public String selectProtocol() {
  1007→        if (members.isEmpty()) {
  1008→            throw new IllegalStateException("Cannot select protocol for empty group");
  1009→        }
  1010→
  1011→        // select the protocol for this group which is supported by all members
  1012→        Set<String> candidates = candidateProtocols();
  1013→
  1014→        // let each member vote for one of the protocols
  1015→        Map<String, Integer> votesByProtocol = new HashMap<>();
  1016→        allMembers().stream().map(member -> member.vote(candidates))
  1017→            .forEach(protocolName -> {
  1018→                int count = votesByProtocol.getOrDefault(protocolName, 0);
  1019→                votesByProtocol.put(protocolName, count + 1);
  1020→            });
  1021→
  1022→        // choose the one with the most votes
  1023→        return votesByProtocol.entrySet().stream()
  1024→            .max(Comparator.comparingInt(Map.Entry::getValue))
  1025→            .map(Map.Entry::getKey).orElse(null);
  1026→    }
  1027→

  1029→     * Increment the protocol count for all of the member's
  1030→     *

   850→        if (subscribedRegularExpressions.isEmpty()) {
   851→            // If the members do not use regular expressions, the subscription is
   852→            // considered as homogeneous if all the members are subscribed to the
   853→            // same topics. Otherwise, it is considered as heterogeneous.
   854→            for (SubscriptionCount subscriberCount : subscribedTopicNames.values()) {
   855→                if (subscriberCount.byNameCount != numberOfMembers) {
   856→                    return HETEROGENEOUS;
   857→                }
   858→            }
   859→            return HOMOGENEOUS;
   860→        } else {
   861→            int count = subscribedRegularExpressions.values().iterator().next();
   862→            if (count == numberOfMembers) {
   863→                // If all the members are subscribed to a single regular expressions
   864→                // and none of them are subscribed to topic names, the subscription
   865→                // is considered as homogeneous. If some members are subscribed to
   866→                // topic names too, the subscription is considered as heterogeneous.
   867→                for (SubscriptionCount subscriberCount : subscribedTopicNames.values()) {
   868→                    if (subscriberCount.byRegexCount != 1 || subscriberCount.byNameCount > 0) {
   869→                        return HETEROGENEOUS;
   870→                    }
   871→                }
   872→                return HOMOGENEOUS;
   873→            } else {
   874→                // The subscription is considered as heterogeneous because
   875→                // there is a mix of regular expressions.
   876→                return SubscriptionType.HETEROGENEOUS;
   877→            }
   878→        }
   879→    }

Perfect! I've completed the analysis and created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've identified all the Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the consumer group coordinator's state machine, including the Join, Sync, and Rebalance states and their transitions.

### Key Files Found:

1. **ClassicGroupState.java** - Defines the group state enum with PREPARING_REBALANCE (Join), COMPLETING_REBALANCE (Sync), and STABLE states
2. **ClassicGroup.java** - Implements state transitions with validation
3. **ConsumerGroup.java** - Modern protocol group states (ASSIGNING, RECONCILING)
4. **GroupMetadataManager.java** - Core handlers for join, sync, and rebalance operations
5. **MemberState.java** - Member-level reconciliation states
6. Multiple supporting files for state orchestration and member management

### State Machine Phases:

- **Join Phase**: Triggered by JoinGroup requests → PREPARING_REBALANCE state
- **Sync Phase**: Members synchronize assignments → COMPLETING_REBALANCE state  
- **Rebalance Phase**: Triggered by member failures/leaves → back to PREPARING_REBALANCE
- **Stable State**: Normal operation with no active rebalance

The answer file includes 15 files, 14 symbols representing key state definitions and methods, and a call chain showing the flow from join through sync to rebalance, along with a detailed narrative explaining the complete state machine architecture.

This state\n     * also represents groups which use Kafka only for offset commits and have no members.\n     *\n     * action: respond normally to join group from new members\n     *         respond to sync group with UNKNOWN_MEMBER_ID\n     *         respond to heartbeat with UNKNOWN_MEMBER_ID\n     *         respond to leave group with UNKNOWN_MEMBER_ID\n     *         respond to offset commit with UNKNOWN_MEMBER_ID\n     *         allow offset fetch requests\n     * transition: last offsets removed in periodic expiration task => DEAD\n     *             join group from a new member => PREPARING_REBALANCE\n     *             group is removed by partition emigration => DEAD\n     *             group is removed by expiration => DEAD\n     */\n    EMPTY(\"Empty\"),\n\n    /**\n     * Group is preparing to rebalance.\n     *\n     * action: respond to heartbeats with REBALANCE_IN_PROGRESS\n     *         respond to sync group with REBALANCE_IN_PROGRESS\n     *         remove member on leave group request\n     *         park join group requests from new or existing members until all expected members have joined\n     *         allow offset commits from previous generation\n     *         allow offset fetch requests\n     * transition: some members have joined by the timeout => COMPLETING_REBALANCE\n     *             all members have left the group => EMPTY\n     *             group is removed by partition emigration => DEAD\n     */\n    PREPARING_REBALANCE(\"PreparingRebalance\"),\n\n    /**\n     * Group is awaiting state assignment from the leader.\n     *\n     * action: respond to heartbeats with REBALANCE_IN_PROGRESS\n     *         respond to offset commits with REBALANCE_IN_PROGRESS\n     *         park sync group requests from followers until transition to STABLE\n     *         allow offset fetch requests\n     * transition: sync group with state assignment received from leader => STABLE\n     *             join group from new member or existing member with updated metadata => PREPARING_REBALANCE\n     *             leave group from existing member => PREPARING_REBALANCE\n     *             member failure detected => PREPARING_REBALANCE\n     *             group is removed by partition emigration => DEAD\n     */\n    COMPLETING_REBALANCE(\"CompletingRebalance\"),\n\n    /**\n     * Group is stable.\n     *\n     * action: respond to member heartbeats normally\n     *         respond to sync group from any member with current assignment\n     *         respond to join group from followers with matching metadata with current group metadata\n     *         allow offset commits from member of current generation\n     *         allow offset fetch requests\n     * transition: member failure detected via heartbeat => subscription.userData().duplicate() : null);\n\n        List<TopicPartition> ownedPartitions = new ArrayList<>(subscription.ownedPartitions());\n        ownedPartitions.sort(Comparator.comparing(TopicPartition::topic).thenComparing(TopicPartition::partition));\n        ConsumerProtocolSubscription.TopicPartition partition = null;\n        for (TopicPartition tp : ownedPartitions) {\n            if (partition == null || !partition.topic().equals(tp.topic())) {\n                partition = new ConsumerProtocolSubscription.TopicPartition().setTopic(tp.topic());\n                data.ownedPartitions().add(partition);\n            }\n            partition.partitions().add(tp.partition());\n        }\n        subscription.rackId().ifPresent(data::setRackId);\n\n        data.setGenerationId(subscription.generationId().orElse(-1));\n        return MessageUtil.toVersionPrefixedByteBuffer(version, data);\n    }\n\n    public static Subscription deserializeSubscription(final ByteBuffer buffer, short version) {\n        version = checkSubscriptionVersion(version);\n\n        try {\n            ConsumerProtocolSubscription data =\n                new ConsumerProtocolSubscription(new ByteBufferAccessor(buffer), version);\n\n            List<TopicPartition> ownedPartitions = new ArrayList<>();\n            for (ConsumerProtocolSubscription.TopicPartition tp : data.ownedPartitions()) {\n                for (Integer partition : tp.partitions()) {\n                    ownedPartitions.add(new TopicPartition(tp.topic(), partition));\n                }\n            }\n\n            return new Subscription(\n                data.topics(),\n                data.userData() != null ? ],\n  \"text\": \"The consumer group coordinator's state machine is implemented across multiple Java source files in the apache/kafka group-coordinator module. The state machine defines three primary protocol phases: Join, Sync, and Rebalance.\\n\\n## State Machine Architecture\\n\\n### Core State Definitions\\n\\n**ClassicGroupState.java** defines the group-level state enum for the classic consumer group protocol with five states:\\n- EMPTY: Group has no members\\n- PREPARING_REBALANCE: Join phase - members are joining and waiting\\n- COMPLETING_REBALANCE: Sync phase - members synchronizing assignments\\n- STABLE: Normal operation\\n- DEAD: Group being removed\\n\\nThe state machine also defines valid state transitions through the `validPreviousStates()` method, which enforces the protocol flow.\\n\\n**ConsumerGroup.java** implements the modern consumer group protocol (KIP-848) with a different state progression:\\n- EMPTY -> ASSIGNING -> RECONCILING -> STABLE\\nThese states more directly correspond to the join/sync phases.\\n\\n### State Transition Implementation\\n\\n**ClassicGroup.java** implements the `transitionTo()` method that performs state transitions with validation. The method calls `assertValidTransition()` to ensure only valid state transitions occur according to the state machine definition.\\n\\n### Join Phase Operations\\n\\n**GroupMetadataManager.java** implements the join phase through multiple methods:\\n- `classicGroupJoin()`: Public entry point for handling JoinGroup requests\\n- `classicGroupJoinToClassicGroup()`: Routes join requests to classic groups\\n- `classicGroupJoinNewMember()`: Handles new member joins\\n- `classicGroupJoinExistingMember()`: Handles existing member rejoin\\n- `classicGroupJoinNewStaticMember()` / `classicGroupJoinNewDynamicMember()`: Specific member type handling\\n- `maybeCompleteJoinPhase()`: Detects when all members have joined\\n- `completeClassicGroupJoin()`: Transitions from PREPARING_REBALANCE to COMPLETING_REBALANCE\\n\\nDuring the join phase, the group state transitions to PREPARING_REBALANCE where members wait for all expected members to join.\\n\\n### Sync Phase Operations\\n\\n**GroupMetadataManager.java** implements the sync phase through:\\n- `classicGroupSync()`: Public entry point for handling SyncGroup requests\\n- `schedulePendingSync()`: Schedules sync operations\\n- Sync operations transition the group from COMPLETING_REBALANCE to STABLE\\n\\nThe sync phase waits for all members to submit their synchronized assignments before transitioning to STABLE state.\\n\\n### Rebalance Phase\\n\\nThe rebalance phase is triggered when:\\n- A member fails (detected via heartbeat timeout)\\n- A member leaves the group\\n- A member sends a new JoinGroup with updated metadata\\n- New members join during STABLE state\\n\\nThese events cause a transition back to PREPARING_REBALANCE, starting a new rebalance cycle.\\n\\n### Member State Management\\n\\n**MemberState.java** defines the member-level reconciliation states:\\n- STABLE: Member is fully reconciled\\n- UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS: Member must revoke some partitions\\n- UNRELEASED_PARTITIONS: Member waiting for partition releases\\n\\n### Support Classes\\n\\n**GroupCoordinatorService.java** and **GroupCoordinatorShard.java** orchestrate the state machine execution across the cluster.\\n\\n**CurrentAssignmentBuilder.java** implements the target assignment building and reconciliation state machine for partition assignment.\\n\\n**ClassicGroupMember.java** and **ConsumerGroupMember.java** track individual member state during protocol phases.\\n\\n## State Transition Flow\\n\\nThe complete state transition chain for a rebalance cycle:\\n\\n1. EMPTY/STABLE \u2192 PREPARING_REBALANCE (join phase triggered)\\n2. PREPARING_REBALANCE \u2192 COMPLETING_REBALANCE (all members joined, ready for sync)\\n3. COMPLETING_REBALANCE \u2192 STABLE (all members synced, rebalance complete)\\n4. STABLE \u2192 PREPARING_REBALANCE (rebalance triggered by event)\\n\\nThese transitions are validated through the ClassicGroupState's state machine definition, ensuring that invalid state transitions cannot occur.\"\n}\n",

The state machine defines three primary protocol phases: Join, Sync, and Rebalance.\\n\\n## State Machine Architecture\\n\\n### Core State Definitions\\n\\n**ClassicGroupState.java** defines the group-level state enum for the classic consumer group protocol with five states:\\n- EMPTY: Group has no members\\n- PREPARING_REBALANCE: Join phase - members are joining and waiting\\n- COMPLETING_REBALANCE: Sync phase - members synchronizing assignments\\n- STABLE: Normal operation\\n- DEAD: Group being removed\\n\\nThe state machine also defines valid state transitions through the `validPreviousStates()` method, which enforces the protocol flow.\\n\\n**ConsumerGroup.java** implements the modern consumer group protocol (KIP-848) with a different state progression:\\n- EMPTY -> ASSIGNING -> RECONCILING -> STABLE\\nThese states more directly correspond to the join/sync phases.\\n\\n### State Transition Implementation\\n\\n**ClassicGroup.java** implements the `transitionTo()` method that performs state transitions with validation. The method calls `assertValidTransition()` to ensure only valid state transitions occur according to the state machine definition.\\n\\n### Join Phase Operations\\n\\n**GroupMetadataManager.java** implements the join phase through multiple methods:\\n- `classicGroupJoin()`: Public entry point for handling JoinGroup requests\\n- `classicGroupJoinToClassicGroup()`: Routes join requests to classic groups\\n- `classicGroupJoinNewMember()`: Handles new member joins\\n- `classicGroupJoinExistingMember()`: Handles existing member rejoin\\n- `classicGroupJoinNewStaticMember()` / `classicGroupJoinNewDynamicMember()`: Specific member type handling\\n- `maybeCompleteJoinPhase()`: Detects when all members have joined\\n- `completeClassicGroupJoin()`: Transitions from PREPARING_REBALANCE to COMPLETING_REBALANCE\\n\\nDuring the join phase, the group state transitions to PREPARING_REBALANCE where members wait for all expected members to join.\\n\\n### Sync Phase Operations\\n\\n**GroupMetadataManager.java** implements the sync phase through:\\n- `classicGroupSync()`: Public entry point for handling SyncGroup requests\\n- `schedulePendingSync()`: Schedules sync operations\\n- Sync operations transition the group from COMPLETING_REBALANCE to STABLE\\n\\nThe sync phase waits for all members to submit their synchronized assignments before transitioning to STABLE state.\\n\\n### Rebalance Phase\\n\\nThe rebalance phase is triggered when:\\n- A member fails (detected via heartbeat timeout)\\n- A member leaves the group\\n- A member sends a new JoinGroup with updated metadata\\n- New members join during STABLE state\\n\\nThese events cause a transition back to PREPARING_REBALANCE, starting a new rebalance cycle.\\n\\n### Member State Management\\n\\n**MemberState.java** defines the member-level reconciliation states:\\n- STABLE: Member is fully reconciled\\n- UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS: Member must revoke some partitions\\n- UNRELEASED_PARTITIONS: Member waiting for partition releases\\n\\n### Support Classes\\n\\n**GroupCoordinatorService.java** and **GroupCoordinatorShard.java** orchestrate the state machine execution across the cluster.\\n\\n**CurrentAssignmentBuilder.java** implements the target assignment building and reconciliation state machine for partition assignment.\\n\\n**ClassicGroupMember.java** and **ConsumerGroupMember.java** track individual member state during protocol phases.\\n\\n## State Transition Flow\\n\\nThe complete state transition chain for a rebalance cycle:\\n\\n1. EMPTY/STABLE \u2192 PREPARING_REBALANCE (join phase triggered)\\n2. PREPARING_REBALANCE \u2192 COMPLETING_REBALANCE (all members joined, ready for sync)\\n3. COMPLETING_REBALANCE \u2192 STABLE (all members synced, rebalance complete)\\n4.
